         <h2><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/push-notifications-with-ionic-and-amazon-pinpoint/" property="url" rel="bookmark"><span property="name headline">Push Notifications with Ionic and Amazon Pinpoint</span></a></h2> 
         <footer class="meta">
           by 
          <span property="author" typeof="Person"><span property="name">Richard Threlkeld</span></span> | on 
          <time property="datePublished" datetime="2017-09-15T08:58:00+00:00">15 SEP 2017</time> | in 
          <span class="categories"><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/messaging/amazon-pinpoint-messaging/" title="View all posts in Amazon Pinpoint"><span property="articleSection">Amazon Pinpoint</span></a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/angularjs/" title="View all posts in AngularJS"><span property="articleSection">AngularJS</span></a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/aws-mobile/" title="View all posts in AWS Mobile"><span property="articleSection">AWS Mobile</span></a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/cordova/" title="View all posts in Cordova"><span property="articleSection">Cordova</span></a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/engagement/" title="View all posts in Engagement"><span property="articleSection">Engagement</span></a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/ionic/" title="View all posts in Ionic"><span property="articleSection">Ionic</span></a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/mobile-engagement/" title="View all posts in Mobile Engagement"><span property="articleSection">Mobile Engagement</span></a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/mobile-hub/" title="View all posts in Mobile Hub"><span property="articleSection">Mobile Hub</span></a></span> | 
          <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/push-notifications-with-ionic-and-amazon-pinpoint/" property="url">Permalink</a> |

          <a href="#" role="button" data-share-dialog=""><span class="span icon-share"></span>&nbsp;Share</a> 
          <div class="share-dialog" style="display: none;">

            <li><a href="https://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;title=Push%20Notifications%20with%20Ionic%20and%20Amazon%20Pinpoint&amp;source=Amazon%20Web%20Services&amp;summary=Engaging%20your%20customers%20through%20communication%20channels%20such%20as%20push%20notifications%20is%20important%20for%20mobile%20app%20success.%20AWS%20services%20such%20as%20AWS%20Mobile%20Hub%20and%20Amazon%20Pinpoint%20enable%20you%20to%20do%20this%20in%20a%20scalable%20and%20cost%20effective%20manner.%20When%20using%20these%20services%20with%20development%20tooling%20like%20Ionic%20Framework%20you%20can%20rapidly%20develop%20modern%20applications%20to%20%5B%26hellip%3B%5D&amp;url=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/push-notifications-with-ionic-and-amazon-pinpoint/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share on LinkedIn"><span class="icon-linkedin-square"></span></a></li>

            <li class="share-dialog-url"><input type="text" value="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/push-notifications-with-ionic-and-amazon-pinpoint/" title="Link to Push Notifications with Ionic and Amazon Pinpoint" readonly></li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
         </footer> 
         <section property="articleBody"> 
          <p>Engaging your customers through communication channels such as push notifications is important for mobile app success. AWS services such as AWS Mobile Hub and Amazon Pinpoint enable you to do this in a scalable and cost effective manner. When using these services with development tooling like <a href="https://ionicframework.com">Ionic Framework</a> you can rapidly develop modern applications to build your business.</p> 
          <p>Ionic <a href="http://blog.ionic.io/sunsetting-ionic-cloud-push-and-auth/">recently announced</a> that they are sunsetting their Push and Auth services. We recently <a href="https://github.com/awslabs/aws-mobile-ionic-sample">launched an Ionic Starter Project</a> and posted <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/user-sign-in-and-sign-up-for-ionic-mobile-apps-with-amazon-cognito/">a tutorial for adding sign-up and sign-in to an Ionic project</a> to help customers evaluate AWS as an alternative for migration. In this post, we cover how to add push notifications to your Ionic project with Amazon Pinpoint.</p> 
          <p>In this tutorial, we show how to add push notifications with Google Cloud Messaging (GCM). A similar procedure can be followed for Apple Push Notification service (APNs) which you can find <a href="http://help.apple.com/xcode/mac/current/#/dev11b059073">on the Apple Developer website</a>.</p> 
          <p> <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/push-notifications-with-ionic-and-amazon-pinpoint/#more-1222" class="more-link"><span aria-label="Continue reading Push Notifications with Ionic and Amazon Pinpoint">(more)</span></a></p> 
         </section> 
        </article> 
        <article class="post" vocab="http://schema.org/" typeof="TechArticle"> 
         <meta property="inLanguage" content="en-US"> 
         <h2><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/user-sign-in-and-sign-up-for-ionic-mobile-apps-with-amazon-cognito/" property="url" rel="bookmark"><span property="name headline">User Sign-in and Sign-up for Ionic Mobile Apps with Amazon Cognito</span></a></h2> 
         <footer class="meta">
           by 
          <span property="author" typeof="Person"><span property="name">Adrian Hall</span></span> | on 
          <time property="datePublished" datetime="2017-09-05T09:24:24+00:00">05 SEP 2017</time> | in 
          <span class="categories"><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/mobile-services/amazon-cognito/" title="View all posts in Amazon Cognito"><span property="articleSection">Amazon Cognito</span></a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/aws-mobile/" title="View all posts in AWS Mobile"><span property="articleSection">AWS Mobile</span></a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/mobile-services/aws-mobile-hub/" title="View all posts in AWS Mobile Hub"><span property="articleSection">AWS Mobile Hub</span></a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/mobile-hub/" title="View all posts in Mobile Hub"><span property="articleSection">Mobile Hub</span></a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/mobile-web/" title="View all posts in Mobile Web"><span property="articleSection">Mobile Web</span></a></span> | 
          <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/user-sign-in-and-sign-up-for-ionic-mobile-apps-with-amazon-cognito/" property="url">Permalink</a> | 
          <a id="aws-comment-trigger-1185" href="https://commenting.awsblogs.com/embed.html?disqus_shortname=aws-mobile-blog&amp;disqus_identifier=1185&amp;disqus_title=User+Sign-in+and+Sign-up+for+Ionic+Mobile+Apps+with+Amazon+Cognito&amp;disqus_url=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/user-sign-in-and-sign-up-for-ionic-mobile-apps-with-amazon-cognito/" data-sandbox-attr="allow-forms allow-scripts allow-popups allow-same-origin" property="discussionUrl"><i class="icon-comment"></i> Comments</a>

            <li><a href="mailto:?subject=User%20Sign-in%20and%20Sign-up%20for%20Ionic%20Mobile%20Apps%20with%20Amazon%20Cognito&amp;body=User%20Sign-in%20and%20Sign-up%20for%20Ionic%20Mobile%20Apps%20with%20Amazon%20Cognito%0A%0Ahttps://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/user-sign-in-and-sign-up-for-ionic-mobile-apps-with-amazon-cognito/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share via email"><span class="icon-envelope-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li class="share-dialog-url"><input type="text" value="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/user-sign-in-and-sign-up-for-ionic-mobile-apps-with-amazon-cognito/" title="Link to User Sign-in and Sign-up for Ionic Mobile Apps with Amazon Cognito" readonly></li> 
           </ul>

         <section property="articleBody"> 
          <p>This post was written by Brice Pelle, AWS Technical Account Manager.</p> 
          <p>In our <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/deploy-and-secure-rest-based-mobile-apps-with-aws-mobile-hub/">previous blog post</a>, we described how to secure and deploy RESTful interfaces for the <a href="https://ionicframework.com/">Ionic Framework</a> using the AWS SDK for JavaScript and AWS Mobile Hub, with support for authenticated and unauthenticated users. This allows guest users to use your app, with limited privileges, without having an account. When users are ready, they can sign up for an account and sign in. This gives them access to more features in the app. Sign-up and sign-in functionality in a mobile app can be difficult to implement securely and challenging to manage.</p> 
          <p>In this post, we take a deeper look at how <a href="https://console.aws.amazon.com/mobilehub/home">AWS Mobile Hub</a> along with <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/cognito/">Amazon Cognito</a> provide a foundation for user sign-up and sign-in. We describe how these services integrate in your Ionic Framework mobile app. We use the same <a href="https://github.com/awslabs/aws-mobile-ionic-sample">sample app</a> introduced in the previous post to showcase the implementation. Refer to the <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/deploy-and-secure-rest-based-mobile-apps-with-aws-mobile-hub/">previous blog post</a> for instructions on how to deploy backend resources with Mobile Hub and how to launch the app.</p> 
          <p> <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/user-sign-in-and-sign-up-for-ionic-mobile-apps-with-amazon-cognito/#more-1185" class="more-link"><span aria-label="Continue reading User Sign-in and Sign-up for Ionic Mobile Apps with Amazon Cognito">(more)</span></a></p> 
         </section> 
        </article>

            <li><a href="mailto:?subject=Deploy%20and%20Secure%20REST-based%20Mobile%20Apps%20with%20AWS%20Mobile%20Hub&amp;body=Deploy%20and%20Secure%20REST-based%20Mobile%20Apps%20with%20AWS%20Mobile%20Hub%0A%0Ahttps://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/deploy-and-secure-rest-based-mobile-apps-with-aws-mobile-hub/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share via email"><span class="icon-envelope-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li class="share-dialog-url"><input type="text" value="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/deploy-and-secure-rest-based-mobile-apps-with-aws-mobile-hub/" title="Link to Deploy and Secure REST-based Mobile Apps with AWS Mobile Hub" readonly></li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
         </footer> 
         <section property="articleBody"> 
          <p>This post was written by Brice Pelle, AWS Technical Account Manager.</p> 
          <p id="deploying-and-securing-rest-backed-mobile-apps-with-aws-mobile-hub">RESTful APIs are used today to power many mobile apps. Using RESTful interfaces allows developers to decouple the frontend application from the backend systems and provides standard interoperability between the two components. Controlling access to resources can be hard to set up. This usually requires addressing authentication and authorization concerns.</p> 
          <p>In this article, I am going to look at how <a href="https://console.aws.amazon.com/mobilehub/home" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">AWS Mobile Hub</a> helps build a serverless mobile backend that exposes REST interfaces, and uses <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/cognito/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Amazon Cognito</a> to help developers integrate authentication and authorization into an <a href="https://ionicframework.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Ionic v2</a> app. I will be using <a href="https://github.com/awslabs/aws-mobile-ionic-sample" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">a sample app</a>, to demonstrate the implementation. The app is a simple task management app that allows access to authenticated and unauthenticated users. &nbsp;I will cover authentication in <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/user-sign-in-and-sign-up-for-ionic-mobile-apps-with-amazon-cognito/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">the second part of this blog</a>.</p> 
          <p> <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/deploy-and-secure-rest-based-mobile-apps-with-aws-mobile-hub/#more-1148" class="more-link"><span aria-label="Continue reading Deploy and Secure REST-based Mobile Apps with AWS Mobile Hub">(more)</span></a></p> 
         </section> 
        </article>

         <h2><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/building-fine-grained-authorization-using-amazon-cognito-user-pools-groups/" property="url" rel="bookmark"><span property="name headline">Building fine-grained authorization using Amazon Cognito User Pools groups</span></a></h2> 
         <footer class="meta">
           by 
          <span property="author" typeof="Person"><span property="name">Adrian Hall</span></span> | on 
          <time property="datePublished" datetime="2017-08-01T08:13:25+00:00">01 AUG 2017</time> | in

            <li><a href="https://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;title=Building%20fine-grained%20authorization%20using%20Amazon%20Cognito%20User%20Pools%20groups&amp;source=Amazon%20Web%20Services&amp;summary=This%20post%20was%20authored%20by%20Leo%20Drakopoulos%2C%20AWS%20Solutions%20Architect.%20User%20authentication%20and%20authorization%20can%20be%20challenging%20when%20building%20web%20and%20mobile%20apps.%20The%20challenges%20include%20handling%20user%20data%20and%20passwords%2C%20token-based%20authentication%2C%20managing%20fine-grained%20permissions%2C%20scalability%2C%20federation%2C%20and%20more.%20In%20this%20post%2C%20we%20show%20how%20to%20integrate%20authentication%20and%20authorization%20into%20an%20Angular%20web%20%5B%26hellip%3B%5D&amp;url=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/building-fine-grained-authorization-using-amazon-cognito-user-pools-groups/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share on LinkedIn"><span class="icon-linkedin-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li><a href="mailto:?subject=Building%20fine-grained%20authorization%20using%20Amazon%20Cognito%20User%20Pools%20groups&amp;body=Building%20fine-grained%20authorization%20using%20Amazon%20Cognito%20User%20Pools%20groups%0A%0Ahttps://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/building-fine-grained-authorization-using-amazon-cognito-user-pools-groups/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share via email"><span class="icon-envelope-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li class="share-dialog-url"><input type="text" value="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/building-fine-grained-authorization-using-amazon-cognito-user-pools-groups/" title="Link to Building fine-grained authorization using Amazon Cognito User Pools groups" readonly></li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
         </footer> 
         <section property="articleBody"> 
          <p>This post was authored by Leo Drakopoulos, AWS Solutions Architect.</p> 
          <p>User authentication and authorization can be challenging when building web and mobile apps. The challenges include handling user data and passwords, token-based authentication, managing fine-grained permissions, scalability, federation, and more.</p> 
          <p>In this post, we show how to integrate authentication and authorization into an <a href="https://angularjs.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Angular web app</a> by using AWS services. You can use <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/cognito/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Amazon Cognito</a> to control permissions for different user groups in your app. This ensures that users have appropriate access to backend resources, determined by the group they belong to.</p> 
          <p> <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/building-fine-grained-authorization-using-amazon-cognito-user-pools-groups/#more-1045" class="more-link"><span aria-label="Continue reading Building fine-grained authorization using Amazon Cognito User Pools groups">(more)</span></a></p> 
         </section>

         <h2><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/deploying-an-emberjs-mobile-web-application-mobile-hub/" property="url" rel="bookmark"><span property="name headline">Deploying an EmberJS mobile web application with Mobile Hub</span></a></h2> 
         <footer class="meta">
           by 
          <span property="author" typeof="Person"><span property="name">Dennis Hills</span></span> | on

           </ul> 
          </div> 
         </footer> 
         <section property="articleBody"> 
          <p>This post was authored by Michael Labieniec, AWS Sr. Solutions Architect.</p> 
          <p><a href="https://emberjs.com">Ember.js</a> is a popular open source JavaScript framework for developing rich, dynamic web applications. It supports <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dependency_injection">dependancy injection</a> model and has been a is a stable contender in the JavaScript community. Ember.js also ships with its own <a href="https://ember-cli.com">CLI</a> which supports building, testing, and deploying your applications. The Ember CLI supports installing plugins and the bundling of those plugins within your application, it has a built in web server to serve your application locally.</p> 
          <p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/mobilehub">AWS Mobile Hub</a> is an AWS service that guides you through feature selection and configuration, it automatically provisions the AWS services required. Mobile Hub generates working code that helps you integrate the <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/about-aws/whats-new/2017/06/aws-mobile-hub-adds-javascript-hosting-and-streaming-for-application-development-testing-and-production/">AWS SDK for JavaScript</a> with your application in minutes. When using Mobile Hub to develop JavaScript-based applications, JavaScript configuration files as well as a sample web application are generated for you, and placed in your Amazon S3 bucket. These configuration files can then be copied directly to your application environment for use. The files can be continuously updated when your AWS environment changes via Mobile Hub. This is useful for developing JavaScript web applications because your AWS configuration can be dynamically updated by Mobile Hub and your application can immediately realize and support those updates when hosted in Amazon S3.</p> 
          <p> <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/deploying-an-emberjs-mobile-web-application-mobile-hub/#more-1051" class="more-link"><span aria-label="Continue reading Deploying an EmberJS mobile web application with Mobile Hub">(more)</span></a></p> 
         </section> 
        </article> 
        <article class="post" vocab="http://schema.org/" typeof="TechArticle"> 
         <meta property="inLanguage" content="en-US"> 
         <h2><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/integrate-the-aws-sdk-for-javascript-into-a-react-app/" property="url" rel="bookmark"><span property="name headline">Integrate the AWS SDK for JavaScript into a React App</span></a></h2> 
         <footer class="meta">
           by 
          <span property="author" typeof="Person"><span property="name">Adrian Hall</span></span> | on 
          <time property="datePublished" datetime="2017-07-11T06:30:39+00:00">11 JUL 2017</time> | in 
          <span class="categories"><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/aws-mobile/" title="View all posts in AWS Mobile"><span property="articleSection">AWS Mobile</span></a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/mobile-hub/" title="View all posts in Mobile Hub"><span property="articleSection">Mobile Hub</span></a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/category/mobile-web/" title="View all posts in Mobile Web"><span property="articleSection">Mobile Web</span></a></span> | 
          <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/integrate-the-aws-sdk-for-javascript-into-a-react-app/" property="url">Permalink</a> | 
          <a id="aws-comment-trigger-1019" href="https://commenting.awsblogs.com/embed.html?disqus_shortname=aws-mobile-blog&amp;disqus_identifier=1019&amp;disqus_title=Integrate+the+AWS+SDK+for+JavaScript+into+a+React+App&amp;disqus_url=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/integrate-the-aws-sdk-for-javascript-into-a-react-app/" data-sandbox-attr="allow-forms allow-scripts allow-popups allow-same-origin" property="discussionUrl"><i class="icon-comment"></i> Comments</a> 
          <script>
    require(['blog'], function() {
      AWS.Blog.commenting('#aws-comment-trigger-1019');
    });
  </script> | 
          <a href="#" role="button" data-share-dialog=""><span class="span icon-share"></span>&nbsp;Share</a> 
          <div class="share-dialog" style="display: none;"> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://www.facebook.com/sharer/sharer.php?u=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/integrate-the-aws-sdk-for-javascript-into-a-react-app/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share on Facebook"><span class="icon-facebook-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://twitter.com/intent/tweet/?text=Integrate%20the%20AWS%20SDK%20for%20JavaScript%20into%20a%20React%20App&amp;via=awscloud&amp;url=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/integrate-the-aws-sdk-for-javascript-into-a-react-app/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share on Twitter"><span class="icon-twitter-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;title=Integrate%20the%20AWS%20SDK%20for%20JavaScript%20into%20a%20React%20App&amp;source=Amazon%20Web%20Services&amp;summary=In%20our%20last%20blog%20post%2C%20I%20showed%20how%20to%20create%20a%20React%20app%20using%20the%20create-react-app%20tool%20provided%20by%20Facebook%2C%20and%20then%20deploy%20the%20app%20to%20a%20content%20delivery%20network%20driven%20by%20AWS%20Mobile%20Hub%2C%20Amazon%20S3%2C%20and%20Amazon%20CloudFront.%20This%20enables%20you%20to%20produce%20dynamic%20single%20page%20applications%20%28SPAs%29%20and%20serve%20them%20to%20a%20%5B%26hellip%3B%5D&amp;url=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/integrate-the-aws-sdk-for-javascript-into-a-react-app/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share on LinkedIn"><span class="icon-linkedin-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li><a href="mailto:?subject=Integrate%20the%20AWS%20SDK%20for%20JavaScript%20into%20a%20React%20App&amp;body=Integrate%20the%20AWS%20SDK%20for%20JavaScript%20into%20a%20React%20App%0A%0Ahttps://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/integrate-the-aws-sdk-for-javascript-into-a-react-app/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share via email"><span class="icon-envelope-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li class="share-dialog-url"><input type="text" value="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/integrate-the-aws-sdk-for-javascript-into-a-react-app/" title="Link to Integrate the AWS SDK for JavaScript into a React App" readonly></li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
         </footer> 
         <section property="articleBody"> 
          <p>In <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/deploy-a-react-app-to-s3-and-cloudfront-with-aws-mobile-hub/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">our last blog post</a>, I showed how to create a React app using the <tt>create-react-app</tt> tool provided by Facebook, and then deploy the app to a content delivery network driven by <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/mobile/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">AWS Mobile Hub</a>, <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/s3/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Amazon S3</a>, and <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/cloudfront/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Amazon CloudFront</a>. This enables you to produce dynamic single page applications (SPAs) and serve them to a global audience.</p> 
          <p>Very few web apps are static web sites. &nbsp;Ideally, you also deploy a serverless backend that includes identity, database, storage, and custom APIs that provide the dynamic data for your SPA. AWS provides this kind of serverless backend. You can compose this backend by using the <a href="https://console.aws.amazon.com/mobilehub/home" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">AWS Mobile Hub console</a>.&nbsp;You still need to integrate the AWS SDK for JavaScript into your SPA.&nbsp;In this post, we walk through that integration.</p> 
          <h3>Add the AWS SDK for JavaScript to your project</h3> 
          <p>The SDK is distributed via the npm package manager.&nbsp;To install the SDK into your project, use the following command:</p> 
          <pre><code class="lang-bash">npm install save aws-sdk
</code></pre> 
          <p>This downloads the SDK and adds an entry into the <tt>package.json</tt> file so that the SDK is downloaded automatically when it is needed.&nbsp;In addition, any dependencies for the SDK are downloaded and included in your project.</p> 
          <h3>Download the AWS configuration for your project</h3> 
          <p>In <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/deploy-a-react-app-to-s3-and-cloudfront-with-aws-mobile-hub/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">the last article</a>, we showed you how to create an AWS Mobile Hub project and turn on the Hosting and Streaming service.&nbsp;This also generates two files in the Amazon S3 bucket that is created:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li><tt>aws-config.js</tt> is used by browser sessions to configure the SDK.</li> 
           <li><tt>aws-exports.js</tt> is used by SPA applications that are packed (by Webpack, Browserify, or similar tools) to configure the SDK.</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p>You need the <tt>aws-exports.js</tt> file for the React app.&nbsp;You can download this file from the Amazon S3 bucket using either the AWS Mobile Hub console or the AWS CLI.&nbsp;To download via the CLI, use the following:</p> 
          <pre><code class="lang-bash">aws s3 cp s3://bucket/aws-exports.js ./src/aws-exports.js
</code></pre> 
          <p>From the AWS Mobile Hub console:</p> 
          <ol> 
           <li>Sign in to the AWS Mobile Hub console.</li> 
           <li>Choose your project.</li> 
           <li>Choose <strong>Hosting and Streaming</strong>.</li> 
           <li>Click <strong>Download aws-exports.js file</strong>.</li> 
          </ol> 
          <p><img class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-1020" src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/0a57cb53ba59c46fc4b692527a38a87c78d84028/2017/07/07/react-2-1.png" alt="" width="413" height="243"></p> 
          <p>You can (and should) do this before every build.&nbsp;I have included the following in my <tt>package.json</tt>:</p> 
          <pre><code class="lang-json">{
	"scripts": {
		"prebuild": "aws s3 cp s3://${S3BUCKET}/aws-exports.js ./src/aws-exports.js",
		"build": "react-scripts build",
		"deploy": "aws s3 cp ./build s3://${S3BUCKET}/ --recursive",
		"start": "react-scripts start",
		"test": "react-scripts test env=jsdom",
		"eject": "react-scripts eject"
	},
	
}
</code></pre> 
          <p>Set the <tt>S3BUCKET</tt> environment variable and build the React app as follows:</p> 
          <pre><code class="lang-bash"># For MacOS or Linux
export S3BUCKET=reacttestapp-hosting-mobilehub-1234567890
# For Windows cmd
# set S3BUCKET=reacttestapp-hosting-mobilehub-1234567890
# For Windows PowerShell
# $env:S3BUCKET="reacttestapp-hosting-mobilehub-1234567890"

# Now run the build
npm run build
</code></pre> 
          <h3>Integrate the SDK into your app</h3> 
          <p>In each SPA, there is an entry point.&nbsp;The entry point for all apps created by <tt>create-react-app</tt> is the <tt>src/App.js</tt> file.&nbsp;The <tt>create-react-app</tt> tool uses ES2015 modules.&nbsp; This means we can use the <tt>import</tt> keyword to bring in the <tt>aws-exports.js</tt> file:</p> 
          <pre><code class="lang-js">/*
&nbsp;* Import the SDK and Project Configuration
&nbsp;*/
import AWS from 'aws-sdk';
import awsmobile from './aws-exports';

/*
&nbsp;* Configure the SDK to use anonymous identity&nbsp;
&nbsp;*/
AWS.config.update({
&nbsp; region: awsmobile.aws_cognito_region,
&nbsp; credentials: new AWS.CognitoIdentityCredentials({
&nbsp; &nbsp; IdentityPoolId: awsmobile.aws_cognito_identity_pool_id
&nbsp; })
});
</code></pre> 
          <p>In this snippet, we import both the SDK and the configuration of the backend, and then automatically create identity credentials for Amazon Cognito based on the configuration.&nbsp;We can also use this to instantiate an Amazon DynamoDB connection or call an Amazon API Gateway REST endpoint using the SDK.</p> 
          <h3>Whats in the aws-exports.js</h3> 
          <p>The <tt>aws-exports.js</tt> file is a standard JavaScript file that is maintained by AWS Mobile Hub on your behalf.&nbsp;It changes when you add, remove, or edit features within AWS Mobile Hub. An example from one of my apps is below:</p> 
          <pre><code class="lang-js">// WARNING: DO NOT EDIT. This file is Auto-Generated by AWS Mobile Hub. It will be overwritten.

// Copyright 2017 Amazon.com, Inc. or its affiliates (Amazon). All Rights Reserved.
// Code generated by AWS Mobile Hub. Amazon gives unlimited permission to
// copy, distribute and modify it.

// AWS Mobile Hub Project Constants
const awsmobile = {
aws_app_analytics : 'enable',
aws_cognito_identity_pool_id : 'us-east-1:XXXXXXXX-XXXX-XXXX-XXXX-XXXXXXXXXXXX',
aws_cognito_region : 'us-east-1',
aws_content_delivery : 'enable',
aws_content_delivery_bucket : 'XXXXXX-hosting-mobilehub-1234567890',
aws_content_delivery_bucket_region : 'us-east-1',
aws_content_delivery_cloudfront : 'enable',
aws_content_delivery_cloudfront_domain : 'XXXXXXXXXXX.cloudfront.net',
aws_mobile_analytics_app_id : 'XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX',
aws_project_id : XXXXXXXX-XXXX-XXXX-XXXX-XXXXXXXXXXXX ',
aws_project_name : 'XXXXXX,
aws_project_region : 'us-east-1',
aws_resource_name_prefix : 'XXXXXX-mobilehub-1234567890,
}

export default awsmobile;
var AWS = require('aws-sdk');
AWS.config.region = awsmobile.aws_project_region;
AWS.config.update({customUserAgent: 'MobileHub v0.1'});
</code></pre> 
          <p>This project has the following enabled:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>Analytics (from the Messaging and Analytics feature)</li> 
           <li>Hosting and Streaming</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p>You can see the appropriate IDs are available through constants that are then exported as a module.&nbsp;You should never edit this file directly. Instead, change the features within your AWS Mobile Hub project and then copy the file to your source code control again.</p> 
          <h3>Best Practices</h3> 
          <p>We consider the following best practices for integrating the SDK:</p> 
          <ol> 
           <li>Always use the latest version of the SDK.</li> 
           <li>Add the <tt>src/aws-exports.js</tt> file to your <tt>.gitignore</tt> (or similar) file. Do not check this file into your source code repository.</li> 
           <li>Copy the <tt>aws-exports.js</tt> file from your AWS Mobile Hub project during the build phase of your app.</li> 
          </ol> 
          <p>Now that you know how to integrate the SDK into your app, you can start using the AWS SDK for JavaScript to access your AWS services. In future articles, we will explore adding AWS service access to your React app. Until then, please see&nbsp;the <a href="http://docs.aws.amazon.com/sdk-for-javascript/v2/developer-guide/welcome.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">AWS SDK for JavaScript Developer Guide</a>&nbsp;for more details.</p> 
         </section> 
        </article>

         <h2><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/enhanced-javascript-development-with-aws-mobile-hub/" property="url" rel="bookmark"><span property="name headline">Enhanced JavaScript development with AWS Mobile Hub</span></a></h2> 
         <footer class="meta">
           by 
          <span property="author" typeof="Person"><span property="name">Richard Threlkeld</span></span> | on 
          <time property="datePublished" datetime="2017-06-02T10:37:01+00:00">02 JUN 2017</time> | 
          <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/enhanced-javascript-development-with-aws-mobile-hub/" property="url">Permalink</a> | 
          <a id="aws-comment-trigger-901" href="https://commenting.awsblogs.com/embed.html?disqus_shortname=aws-mobile-blog&amp;disqus_identifier=901&amp;disqus_title=Enhanced+JavaScript+development+with+AWS+Mobile+Hub&amp;disqus_url=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/enhanced-javascript-development-with-aws-mobile-hub/" data-sandbox-attr="allow-forms allow-scripts allow-popups allow-same-origin" property="discussionUrl"><i class="icon-comment"></i> Comments</a> 
          <script>
    require(['blog'], function() {
      AWS.Blog.commenting('#aws-comment-trigger-901');
    });
  </script> | 
          <a href="#" role="button" data-share-dialog=""><span class="span icon-share"></span>&nbsp;Share</a> 
          <div class="share-dialog" style="display: none;"> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://www.facebook.com/sharer/sharer.php?u=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/enhanced-javascript-development-with-aws-mobile-hub/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share on Facebook"><span class="icon-facebook-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://twitter.com/intent/tweet/?text=Enhanced%20JavaScript%20development%20with%20AWS%20Mobile%20Hub&amp;via=awscloud&amp;url=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/enhanced-javascript-development-with-aws-mobile-hub/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share on Twitter"><span class="icon-twitter-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;title=Enhanced%20JavaScript%20development%20with%20AWS%20Mobile%20Hub&amp;source=Amazon%20Web%20Services&amp;summary=Introduction%20As%20the%20JavaScript%20ecosystem%20grows%2C%20we%20continue%20to%20invest%20to%20help%20customers%20build%20mobile%20and%20hybrid%20apps.%20Today%2C%20we%20released%20a%20feature%20in%20AWS%20Mobile%20Hub%20called%20Hosting%20and%20Streaming.%20This%20feature%20automates%20deployment%20of%20mobile%20websites%20in%20both%20test%20and%20production%20scenarios%20using%20Amazon%20S3%20and%20Amazon%20CloudFront.%20It%20also%20helps%20developers%20streamline%20%5B%26hellip%3B%5D&amp;url=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/enhanced-javascript-development-with-aws-mobile-hub/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share on LinkedIn"><span class="icon-linkedin-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li><a href="mailto:?subject=Enhanced%20JavaScript%20development%20with%20AWS%20Mobile%20Hub&amp;body=Enhanced%20JavaScript%20development%20with%20AWS%20Mobile%20Hub%0A%0Ahttps://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/enhanced-javascript-development-with-aws-mobile-hub/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share via email"><span class="icon-envelope-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li class="share-dialog-url"><input type="text" value="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/enhanced-javascript-development-with-aws-mobile-hub/" title="Link to Enhanced JavaScript development with AWS Mobile Hub" readonly></li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
         </footer> 
         <section property="articleBody"> 
          <h3 id="toc_1">Introduction</h3> 
          <p>As the JavaScript ecosystem grows, we continue to invest to help customers build mobile and hybrid apps. Today, we released a feature in AWS Mobile Hub called Hosting and Streaming. This feature automates deployment of mobile websites in both test and production scenarios using Amazon S3 and Amazon CloudFront. It also helps developers streamline their configuration workflow with standard configuration files and SDKs.</p> 
          <p>With this new capability JavaScript developers can launch preconfigured AWS architectures or build them from the Mobile Hub project interface. With a single click, developers can create a global website with central configuration settings and pre-downloaded SDKs.</p> 
          <h3 id="toc_2">Overview</h3> 
          <p><img class="alignleft size-medium wp-image-906" src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/0a57cb53ba59c46fc4b692527a38a87c78d84028/2017/06/01/Card-300x198.png" alt="" width="300" height="198">Go to the <a href="https://console.aws.amazon.com/mobilehub/home?region=us-east-1">Mobile Hub console</a> and choose <strong>Create a new Project</strong>, enable some features such as User Sign-in, NoSQL Database or Cloud Logic. Alternatively you can <a href="http://docs.aws.amazon.com/mobile-hub/latest/developerguide/project-import-export.html">import an existing project</a>.</p> 
          <p>Select <strong>Hosting and Streaming</strong> to view the launch page for your hosted Mobile Web application.</p> 
          <p>&nbsp;</p> 
          <p>&nbsp;</p> 
          <p>&nbsp;</p> 
          <p>Choose one of the Launch buttons to run the sample app, either directly from Amazon S3 hosting or from an Amazon CloudFront deployment. The sample is a JavaScript application that makes a sample call to Amazon Cognito demonstrating how to get an identity and credentials.</p> 
          <p><img class="aligncenter wp-image-903 size-large" src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/0a57cb53ba59c46fc4b692527a38a87c78d84028/2017/06/01/Page-1024x763.png" alt="" width="640" height="477"></p> 
          <p>Choose <strong>Manage files</strong>. This takes you to the S3 bucket that AWS Mobile Hub configured with your resources. The resources include the webpage you just launched and the AWS SDK for JavaScript. In addition this directory contains two important files:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>aws-config.js</li> 
           <li>aws-exports.js</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p>These files contain the AWS references for your mobile web or hybrid apps. You can use these references in your JavaScript app when communicating with AWS services. The sample app shows how to use the aws-config.js to make an unauthenticated call to Amazon Cognito. If you configure the User Sign-in feature to <em>require</em> sign-in (this is recommended), then Mobile Hub configures AWS Identity and Access Management policies so that only users with valid authentication can access the other features (like Amazon DynamoDB or Amazon API Gateway) in your project. A good example of this is in the <a href="http://blog.ionic.io/aws-and-ionic-team-up-to-build-the-ultimate-full-stack-starter/">AWS Ionic Starter project</a> launched last month.</p> 
          <p>The aws-exports.js file is a new ECMAScript2015 compliant file we introduced to help you write applications that follow this standard.</p> 
          <h2 id="toc_3">Walkthrough: aws-exports.js with Babel and NodeJS</h2> 
          <p>To get started with aws-exports.js, here is a walkthrough that creates a project which compiles using Babel. The walkthrough then shows how to use the AWS SDK for JavaScript to use these capabilities.</p> 
          <p>Babel is a JavaScript compiler for newer JavaScript language features such as Import and Export statements that are <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Statements/import">standardized in ES2015</a>. You can read more about Babel <a href="http://babeljs.io">here</a>.</p> 
          <p>To get started first <a href="https://docs.npmjs.com/getting-started/installing-node">ensure that you have NodeJS and NPM installed</a>.</p> 
          <p>Next create a project directory with a source and destination location for Babel to read from and write files to. Then, initialize your project:</p> 
          <div> 
           <pre><code class="language-bash">
$mkdir awsmobile
$cd awsmobile
$mkdir dist
$mkdir src
$npm init
</code></pre> 
          </div> 
          <p>Initialize the directory with defaults. Now, install the Babel prerequisites and create an entry point for your code along with the AWS SDK for JavaScript:</p> 
          <div> 
           <pre><code class="language-bash">
$npm install --save-dev babel-cli babel-preset-env aws-sdk
$touch .babelrc
$touch ./src/awstest.js
</code></pre> 
          </div> 
          <p>Edit the <code>.babelrc</code> file with the following code:</p> 
          <pre><code class="language-javascript">{ "presets": ["env"] }
</code></pre> 
          <p>Notice that the <code>awstest.js</code> file is in the <code>./src</code> directory. Edit the <code>awstest.js</code> file using a text editor with the following code:</p> 
          <div> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">

'use strict';
import { awsmobile } from './aws-exports';
console.log(awsmobile);</code></pre> 
          </div> 
          <p>Place <code>aws-exports.js</code> from S3 bucket generated by Mobile Hub into the <code>./src</code> directory. When <code>awstest.js</code> is compiled by Babel, the output will be in the <code>./dist</code> directory. You can execute this with the following commands:</p> 
          <div> 
           <pre><code class="language-bash">$./node_modules/.bin/babel ./src --experimental --source-maps-inline -d ./dist
$node dist/awstest.js</code></pre> 
          </div> 
          <p>If everything worked correctly, your configuration settings for communicating with AWS are printed to the screen.</p> 
          <h3 id="toc_4">Downloading files from Amazon S3 with the AWS SDK for JavaScript and aws-exports.js</h3> 
          <p>Now that youve got the basics of the build process how can you use these settings? Mobile Hub handles all the heavy lifting of configuring AWS Cloud resources. Suppose you want to download a file from the S3 bucket that was created. The following code shows an example of using the <code>aws-exports.js</code> settings file with a simple app that performs a GetObject operation and writes the <code>index.html</code> file as <code>mobilehub.html</code> to your local disk. Modify your <code>./src/awstest.js</code> with the following code:</p> 
          <div> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">
'use strict';

import { awsmobile } from './aws-exports';
import AWS from 'aws-sdk';

//Filestream setup
var fs = require('fs');
var writeStream =  fs.createWriteStream('mobilehub.html');

var s3 = new AWS.S3();
var s3params = ({
    Bucket: awsmobile.aws_content_delivery_bucket,
    Key: 'index.html'
});

var res = s3.getObject(s3params, function(err, res){
    if (err){
        console.error(err);
    }else {
        writeStream.write(res.Body);
    }
})</code></pre> 
          </div> 
          <p>Run the following commands to compile your code and execute:</p> 
          <div> 
           <pre><code class="language-bash">$./node_modules/.bin/babel ./src --experimental --source-maps-inline -d ./dist
$node dist/awstest.js</code></pre> 
          </div> 
          <p>In your root directory, there is now a file called <code>mobilehub.html</code>. This is the downloaded sample page from your S3 bucket.</p> 
          <h3 id="toc_5">Further work</h3> 
          <p>This is a simple example. Look at the other settings available and configure your Mobile Hub project in different ways to see what is available. For instance, you can use this feature to configure Amazon Cognito User Pools or an Amazon API Gateway endpoint backed by AWS Lambda. Let us know what future functionality or examples youd like us to explore in the comments.</p> 
          <p>&nbsp;</p> 
          <p>&nbsp;</p> 
         </section> 
        </article>

         <h2><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/aws-mobile-app-backend-with-hybrid-apps/" property="url" rel="bookmark"><span property="name headline">AWS Mobile App Backend with Hybrid Apps</span></a></h2> 
         <footer class="meta">
           by 
          <span property="author" typeof="Person"><span property="name">Sean Senior</span></span> | on 
          <time property="datePublished" datetime="2016-12-14T14:49:27+00:00">14 DEC 2016</time> | 
          <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/aws-mobile-app-backend-with-hybrid-apps/" property="url">Permalink</a> | 
          <a id="aws-comment-trigger-515" href="https://commenting.awsblogs.com/embed.html?disqus_shortname=aws-mobile-blog&amp;disqus_identifier=515&amp;disqus_title=AWS+Mobile+App+Backend+with+Hybrid+Apps&amp;disqus_url=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/aws-mobile-app-backend-with-hybrid-apps/" data-sandbox-attr="allow-forms allow-scripts allow-popups allow-same-origin" property="discussionUrl"><i class="icon-comment"></i> Comments</a> 
          <script>
    require(['blog'], function() {
      AWS.Blog.commenting('#aws-comment-trigger-515');
    });
  </script> | 
          <a href="#" role="button" data-share-dialog=""><span class="span icon-share"></span>&nbsp;Share</a> 
          <div class="share-dialog" style="display: none;"> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://www.facebook.com/sharer/sharer.php?u=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/aws-mobile-app-backend-with-hybrid-apps/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share on Facebook"><span class="icon-facebook-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://twitter.com/intent/tweet/?text=AWS%20Mobile%20App%20Backend%20with%20Hybrid%20Apps&amp;via=awscloud&amp;url=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/aws-mobile-app-backend-with-hybrid-apps/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share on Twitter"><span class="icon-twitter-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;title=AWS%20Mobile%20App%20Backend%20with%20Hybrid%20Apps&amp;source=Amazon%20Web%20Services&amp;summary=This%20post%20was%20co-authored%20by%20Leo%20Drakopoulos%2C%20AWS%20Solutions%20Architect.%20Today%20we%20would%20like%20to%20tell%20you%20about%20a%20new%20solutions%20brief%20for%20building%20serverless%20mobile%20backend%20solutions%20on%20AWS%2C%20and%20a%20step-by-step%20walkthrough%20for%20implementing%20this%20pattern%2C%20using%20the%20Ionic%20framework%20on%C2%A0AWS%20Answers.%20Like%20other%20solutions%20on%20AWS%20Answers%2C%20this%20one%20was%20built%20by%20%5B%26hellip%3B%5D&amp;url=https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/aws-mobile-app-backend-with-hybrid-apps/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share on LinkedIn"><span class="icon-linkedin-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li><a href="mailto:?subject=AWS%20Mobile%20App%20Backend%20with%20Hybrid%20Apps&amp;body=AWS%20Mobile%20App%20Backend%20with%20Hybrid%20Apps%0A%0Ahttps://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/aws-mobile-app-backend-with-hybrid-apps/" target="_blank" aria-label="Share via email"><span class="icon-envelope-square"></span></a></li> 
            <li class="share-dialog-url"><input type="text" value="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/mobile/aws-mobile-app-backend-with-hybrid-apps/" title="Link to AWS Mobile App Backend with Hybrid Apps" readonly></li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
         </footer> 
         <section property="articleBody"> 
          <p><em>This post was co-authored by Leo Drakopoulos, AWS Solutions Architect.</em></p> 
          <p>Today we would like to tell you about a new solutions brief for building serverless mobile backend solutions on AWS, and a step-by-step walkthrough for implementing this pattern, using the Ionic framework on&nbsp;<a href="https://aws.amazon.com/answers/" target="_blank">AWS Answers</a>. Like other solutions on AWS Answers, this one was built by AWS Solutions Architects. This solution incorporates best practices for deploying scalable backend services for mobile applications by leveraging AWS managed services.</p> 
          <p>The <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/answers/mobile/aws-mobile-app-backend/" target="_blank">Mobile Backend Services brief</a> provides best practices, architectural guidance, and considerations for using managed services on the AWS Cloud to simplify development of RESTful backend services for mobile apps. The <a href="https://s3.amazonaws.com/solutions-reference/mobile-backend/latest/mobile-app-backend.pdf" target="_blank">walkthrough</a> shows you how to power hybrid mobile applications built using the Ionic Framework. You can use the walkthrough guide to quickly integrate your hybrid mobile application with mobile backend services hosted on AWS. The reference architecture and walkthrough enable you to deploy your Ionic mobile app without having to manage any backend infrastructure. The same general approach can be applied to any framework built using JavaScript, such as PhoneGap/Cordova, Framework 7, etc. Heres how it looks:</p> 
          <p style="text-align: center"><img class="alignnone wp-image-524 size-full" src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/0a57cb53ba59c46fc4b692527a38a87c78d84028/2016/12/14/mobile-app-backend-architecture-blog-1.png" alt="" width="1926" height="702"></p> 
          <p>This mobile app backend design applies to both hybrid and native mobile application use cases, including the following:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>User sign in and registration</li> 
           <li>Saving and retrieving data from a NoSQL store</li> 
           <li>Calling cloud hosted REST APIs from your hybrid mobile application</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p>To enable these use cases, the solution uses Amazon Cognito User Pools to add sign-up, sign-in, and user management for mobile apps. Amazon API Gateway is used to create custom RESTful APIs. These APIs trigger an AWS Lambda function to perform CRUD operations on an Amazon DynamoDB NoSQL data store.</p> 
          <p>Here is how it works. An Amazon Cognito User Pool authorizer is associated with a RESTful API hosted in Amazon API Gateway. The authorizer authenticates every API call made from a mobile app by leveraging a JSON Web Token (JWT) passed in the API call headers. Amazon API Gateway is natively integrated with Amazon Cognito User Pools so the validation of the JWT requires no additional effort from the application developer. Amazon API Gateway then invokes an AWS Lambda function that accesses other AWS services, which in this case is Amazon DynamoDB. When AWS Lambda is invoked, it assumes an AWS Identity and Access Management (IAM) role. The IAM role determines the level of access that AWS Lambda has to Amazon DynamoDB.</p> 
          <p>The cost to run this reference implementation in production varies, depending on the scale of your backend services. Some of the services leveraged by the solution are part of the AWS Free Tier, which enables you to get started at a very low cost point. For more information, see AWS Free Tier at <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/free/" target="_blank">https://aws.amazon.com/free/</a>.</p> 
          <p>The solution brief for the <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/answers/mobile/aws-mobile-app-backend/" target="_blank">Mobile App Backend</a> is available online or you can download the .pdf version <a href="https://d0.awsstatic.com/aws-answers/aws-mobile-app-backend.pdf" target="_blank">here</a>. You can get started today by downloading the <a href="https://s3.amazonaws.com/solutions-reference/mobile-backend/latest/mobile-app-backend.pdf" target="_blank">step-by-step walkthrough guide</a> for the reference implementation using the Ionic framework.</p> 
         </section> 
        </article>

          </div> 
         </footer> 
         <section property="articleBody"> 
          <h1>Introduction</h1> 
          <p>Modern authentication flows incorporate new challenge types, in addition to a password, to verify the identity of users. For example, these challenge types include CAPTCHAs or dynamic challenge questions. With Amazon Cognito Your User Pools, we now have a flexible authentication flow that you can customize to incorporate additional authentication methods and support dynamic authentication flows that are server driven. First, we generalize authentication into two common steps, which are implemented through two APIs (<span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">InitiateAuth</span> and <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">RespondToAuthChallenge</span>). In this flow, a user authenticates by answering successive challenges until authentication either fails or the user is issued tokens. With these two steps, which can be repeated to include different challenges, we support any custom authentication flow. Second, we provide the ability to customize your authentication flow with AWS Lambda triggers. These triggers issue and verify their own challenges as part of the authentication flow.</p> 
          <p>In this post, we provide detail on the two APIs and their inputs and outputs as we demonstrate how you can customize Your User Pools authentication flow to contain additional challenges such as CAPTCHAs.</p> 
          <h1>New APIs</h1> 
          <h2>InitiateAuth</h2> 
          <p>This API kicks off the authentication flow. It explicitly indicates to Amazon Cognito how you are trying to authenticate, along with initial authentication parameters that are passed to the pre-authentication Lambda trigger. With a successful call, the response provides either tokens (for an authenticated user) or a challenge.</p> 
          <p>The <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">InitiateAuth</span> API has the following inputs:</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">AuthFlow String</span></p> 
          <p>The name of the auth flow is determined by the service. The following are supported: USER_SRP_AUTH, REFRESH_TOKEN_AUTH, CUSTOM_AUTH, ADMIN_NO_SRP_AUTH. USER_SRP_AUTH and REFRESH_TOKEN_AUTH were previously available through other APIs but they are easier to use with the new APIs. For a custom authentication flow, the CUSTOM_AUTH value is provided. For more information on the flows, see <a href="http://docs.aws.amazon.com/cognito/latest/developerguide/amazon-cognito-user-pools-authentication-flow.html" target="_blank">Custom Authentication Flow</a> in the <em>Amazon Cognito Developer Guide</em>.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">AuthParameters Map of String, String</span></p> 
          <p>Key/value pairs containing all of the inputs necessary to initiate this authentication method (e.g., USERNAME=johndoe, SRP_A=AB009809). Based on authentication flow and a combination of some parameters missing, authentication can be failed.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">[ClientMetadata] Map of String, String</span></p> 
          <p>Optional field. Key/value pairs containing inputs that arent authentication parameters but are inputs to the pre-authentication Lambda trigger. Using this Lambda trigger, you can implement custom validations to accept/deny the request, based on, for example, the user context.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">ClientId String</span></p> 
          <p>The app clientId for the app attempting to authenticate.</p> 
          <h2>RespondToAuthChallenge</h2> 
          <p>Used to respond to challenges, which can include multiple rounds until the user successfully authenticates (and Amazon Cognito issues tokens) or fails. You have control over how many challenge rounds are presented to the user. This can be decided based on the challenges already answered. With each call, the response is either a successful authentication when tokens are issued, a new challenge, or failure of the authentication.</p> 
          <p>The <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">RespondToAuthChallenge</span> API has the following inputs:</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">ChallengeName String</span></p> 
          <p>Name of the challenge being responded to.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">Session String</span></p> 
          <p>An encrypted session received by the client in the previous step that the client must pass back as-is. The session contains state information about the current authentication. It cannot be replayed and it expires after 3 minutes.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">ChallengeResponses Map of String, String</span></p> 
          <p>Key/value pairs containing all of the parameters necessary to respond to the challenge (e.g., captchaAnswer=AZ235F).</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">ClientId String</span></p> 
          <p>ClientId trying to authenticate.</p> 
          <h2>InitiateAuth and RespondToAuthChallenge outputs</h2> 
          <p>A successful call to either of the APIs results in tokens that indicate that the authentication flow is complete, or a challenge with a session and parameters.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">AuthenticationResult containing Tokens<br> </span></p> 
          <p>If this is the last step in the authentication flow, the result contains ID, access and refresh tokens. For more information, see <a href="http://docs.aws.amazon.com/cognito/latest/developerguide/amazon-cognito-user-pools-using-tokens-with-identity-providers.html" target="_blank">Using Tokens with User Pools</a> in the <em>Amazon Cognito Developer Guide</em>.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">ChallengeName String</span></p> 
          <p>Name of the next challenge. For example, possible values can be CUSTOM_CHALLENGE, if a custom challenge needs to be answered, or PASSWORD_VERIFIER, if password verification is required.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">Session String</span></p> 
          <p>An encrypted session received by the client in the previous step that the client must pass back as-is. The session contains state information about the current authentication. It cannot be replayed and it expires after 3 minutes.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">ChallengeParameters Map of String, String</span></p> 
          <p>Key/value pairs containing all of the parameters necessary to prompt the user for the returned challenge (e.g., captchaUrl=<a href="https://xyz.com/captcha/123415">https://xyz.com/captcha/123415</a>).</p> 
          <h1>Diving into the custom authentication flow</h1> 
          <p>To provide you control over the authentication flow, we introduced a flow of CUSTOM_AUTH type and provided you with Lambda triggers you can use to implement this custom authentication flow. The flow can be broken down into the following decisions that you can customize through Lambda triggers:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>Analyze the challenges a user has answered so far (successfully or unsuccessfully) and then succeed the authentication (and generate tokens), fail authentication, or prompt the user with a new challenge. This is called the Define Auth Challenge Lambda trigger.</li> 
           <li>Generate a challenge that consists of parameters used to challenge the user and valid answers that can be used when the challenge is answered. This is called the Create Auth Challenge Lambda trigger.</li> 
           <li>Verify if the answer provided by the user is valid. This is called the Verify Auth Challenge Lambda trigger.</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p>Lambda triggers can be entered as code in the AWS Lambda console as shown.</p> 
          <p><img class="alignnone wp-image-351 size-full" src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/0a57cb53ba59c46fc4b692527a38a87c78d84028/2016/10/24/lambda_console.png" alt="lambda_console" width="797" height="713"></p> 
          <p>You can configure Lambda triggers in the Amazon Cognito console on the User Pools Triggers page as shown next. When a Lambda trigger is selected in the Amazon Cognito console, the necessary execution rights are created automatically by the console.</p> 
          <p><img class="alignnone wp-image-357 size-full" src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/0a57cb53ba59c46fc4b692527a38a87c78d84028/2016/10/24/configure_lambda.png" alt="configure_lambda" width="975" height="646"></p> 
          <p>When an app initiates a flow of CUSTOM_AUTH type, Amazon Cognito executes the Define Auth Challenge Lambda trigger to issue a challenge type. This can be a standard (built-in) challenge, such as SRP, that can be handled by the Amazon Cognito service. Or it can be a custom challenge handled by a Lambda trigger that you supply (CUSTOM_CHALLENGE type). In general, this process takes as input the past challenges answered by the user and their result. If the challenge issued is of custom type, Amazon Cognito calls a Lambda trigger to create and issue the challenge. The Lambda trigger passes back the challenge parameters and valid answers. This process is shown in the following two diagrams.</p> 
          <p><img class="alignnone wp-image-358 size-full" src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/0a57cb53ba59c46fc4b692527a38a87c78d84028/2016/10/24/diagram_1.png" alt="diagram_1" width="975" height="596"></p> 
          <p><img class="alignnone wp-image-359 size-full" src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/0a57cb53ba59c46fc4b692527a38a87c78d84028/2016/10/24/diagram_2.png" alt="diagram_2" width="975" height="594"></p> 
          <p>Amazon Cognito User Pools passes the challenge and an encrypted piece of session information back to the client SDK. The client SDK gathers the answers to the challenge and passes back the answers and the encrypted session data as it received it. Amazon Cognito User Pools decrypts the data and calls a Lambda trigger to check if the answers match. Amazon Cognito User Pools then calls the Lambda trigger with the challenges answered so far (adding the challenge just answered). The Lambda trigger can issue a new challenge, issue tokens, or fail authentication, and the process can repeat accordingly. We dive deep into the Lambda contract specifications next.</p> 
          <h1>Lambda Trigger contract specifications</h1> 
          <p>There are three Lambda triggers mentioned previously. We provide detail on the different parameters the Lambda triggers take as inputs and the valid outputs. All three of these Lambda triggers also receive all of the users attributes as inputs.</p> 
          <h2>DefineAuthChallenge: The challenges (state machine) Lambda trigger</h2> 
          <p>This Lambda trigger has as input the unencrypted session challenge answering information (it was decrypted by the service after it was passed to and from the client). The trigger then returns a challenge name or a Boolean value that indicates whether Amazon Cognito should issue tokens or not.</p> 
          <h3>Inputs</h3> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">session List of ChallengeResult objects</span></p> 
          <p>This is a list containing <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">ChallengeResult</span> objects that indicate whether the challenge was successfully answered. A <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">ChallengeResult</span> object contains a challenge name (<span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeName</span>), a Boolean value with the challenge answering result (<span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeResult</span>), and challenge metadata that you populate when you generate a challenge (<span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeMetadata</span>).</p> 
          <h3>Outputs</h3> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeName String</span></p> 
          <p>Amazon Cognito returns a new challenge name that the client must answer. Alternatively, Amazon Cognito can issue tokens or fail authentication using the following parameters. If you want to generate a challenge with the Create Auth Challenge Lambda trigger, your trigger must output a <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeName</span> of CUSTOM_CHALLENGE.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">issueTokens Boolean</span></p> 
          <p>Indicates whether tokens should be issued to the user, which means the user was authenticated.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">failAuthentication Boolean</span></p> 
          <p>Indicates whether the users authentication attempt should be terminated because of a failure to authenticate.</p> 
          <h3>Example Lambda Trigger</h3> 
          <p>This example Lambda trigger issues tokens if SRP_A, PASSWORD_VERIFIER, and CUSTOM_CHALLENGE challenges were passed; otherwise it fails the authentication.</p> 
          <pre><code class="lang-javascript">exports.handler = function(event, context) {
    if (event.request.session.length == 1 &amp;amp;&amp;amp; event.request.session[0].challengeName == 'SRP_A') {
        event.response.issueTokens = false;
        event.response.failAuthentication = false;
        event.response.challengeName = 'PASSWORD_VERIFIER';
    } else if (event.request.session.length == 2 &amp;amp;&amp;amp; event.request.session[1].challengeName == 'PASSWORD_VERIFIER' &amp;amp;&amp;amp; event.request.session[1].challengeResult == true) {
        event.response.issueTokens = false;
        event.response.failAuthentication = false;
        event.response.challengeName = 'CUSTOM_CHALLENGE';
    } else if (event.request.session.length == 3 &amp;amp;&amp;amp; event.request.session[2].challengeName == 'CUSTOM_CHALLENGE' &amp;amp;&amp;amp; event.request.session[2].challengeResult == true) {
        event.response.issueTokens = true;
        event.response.failAuthentication = false;
    } else {
        event.response.issueTokens = false;
        event.response.failAuthentication = true;
    }
    context.done(null, event);
}</code></pre> 
          <h2>CreateAuthChallenge: The challenge generator Lambda trigger</h2> 
          <p>This Lambda trigger takes a challenge name as input and then generates challenge parameters based on that challenge.</p> 
          <h3>Inputs</h3> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeName String</span></p> 
          <p>The name of the challenge the Lambda trigger has been requested to issue.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">session List of ChallengeResult objects</span></p> 
          <p>This is a list containing <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">ChallengeResult</span> objects that indicate whether the challenge was successfully answered. A <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">ChallengeResult</span> object contains a challenge name (<span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeName</span>), a Boolean value with the challenge answering result (<span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeResult</span>), and challenge metadata that you populate when you generate a challenge (<span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeMetadata</span>).</p> 
          <h3>Outputs</h3> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">publicChallengeParameters Map of String, String</span></p> 
          <p>The Lambda trigger returns a map of public challenge parameters. This map is sent to the client unencrypted so that the client can present the challenge to the user; for example, a CAPTCHA URL.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">privateChallengeParameters Map of String, String</span></p> 
          <p>The Lambda trigger returns a map of private challenge parameters that it generates. This output is labeled private and the client cannot see it. For example, it might be used to hold CAPTCHA answer or other valid answers for the challenge.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeMetadata String</span></p> 
          <p>Metadata about the challenge. This data is put in the session of challenge results when this challenge is answered.</p> 
          <h3>Example Lambda trigger</h3> 
          <p>The following Lambda trigger generates the <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">publicChallengeParameters</span> and <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">privateChallengeParameters</span> maps, with the URL to a CAPTCHA in the public map and the valid answer to the CAPTCHA in the private map. The two pieces usually come from an external service.</p> 
          <pre><code class="lang-javascript">exports.handler = function(event, context) {
    if (event.request.session.length == 2 &amp;&amp; event.request.challengeName == 'CUSTOM_CHALLENGE') {
        event.response.publicChallengeParameters = {};
        event.response.publicChallengeParameters.captchaUrl = 'url/123.jpg'
        event.response.privateChallengeParameters = {};
        event.response.privateChallengeParameters.answer = '5';
        event.response.challengeMetadata = 'CAPTCHA_CHALLENGE';
    }
    context.done(null, event);
}</code></pre> 
          <h2>Verify Auth Challenge: The response verifying Lambda Trigger</h2> 
          <p>This Lambda trigger verifies the answers to the challenges. It gets acceptable answers to the challenge, provided by the previous Create Auth Challenge Lambda trigger, and compares them to the client provided answer.</p> 
          <h3>Inputs</h3> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">privateChallengeParameters  Map of String, String</span></p> 
          <p>This input is the same as described previously for the Create Auth Challenge Lambda trigger. Amazon Cognito forwards the map of private challenge parameters from the Create Auth Challenge Lambda trigger to the Verify Auth Challenge Lambda trigger. These parameters include valid answers for the challenge.</p> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeAnswer String</span></p> 
          <p>The answer provided by the user to the challenge.</p> 
          <h3>Outputs</h3> 
          <p><span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">answerCorrect Boolean</span></p> 
          <p>Indicates whether the answer provided to the challenge was correct.</p> 
          <h3>Example Lambda trigger</h3> 
          <p>The following Lambda trigger checks if the <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeAnswer</span> value is equal to an answer entry in the <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">privateChallengeParameters</span> map to determine if the challenge was answered correctly.</p> 
          <pre><code class="lang-javascript">exports.handler = function(event, context) {
    if (event.request.privateChallengeParameters.answer == event.request.challengeAnswer) {
        event.response.answerCorrect = true;
    } else {
        event.response.answerCorrect = false;
    }
    context.done(null, event);
}
</code></pre> 
          <h1>Client SDK considerations</h1> 
          <p>The client SDKs expose a new callback that requests input from users in the case of custom challenges. The <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeParameters</span> parameter is used to present the challenge to the user and the users response is passed back in the <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">challengeResponses</span> parameter to the <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">RespondToAuthChallenge</span> API call. Here is an example in JavaScript to complement the example Lambda triggers described previously. As can be seen in the following, the JavaScript SDK provides a <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">customChallenge</span> callback while the Android and iOS SDKs provide similar callbacks.</p> 
          <pre><code class="lang-javascript">var authenticationData = {
    Username : 'username',
    Password : 'password',
};
var authenticationDetails = new AWSCognito.CognitoIdentityServiceProvider.AuthenticationDetails(authenticationData);
var poolData = { 
    UserPoolId : '...', // Your user pool id here
    ClientId : '...' // Your client id here
};
var userPool = new AWSCognito.CognitoIdentityServiceProvider.CognitoUserPool(poolData);
var userData = {
    Username : 'username',
    Pool : userPool
};
var cognitoUser = new AWSCognito.CognitoIdentityServiceProvider.CognitoUser(userData);
cognitoUser.setAuthenticationFlowType(CUSTOM_AUTH);
cognitoUser.authenticateUser(authenticationDetails, {
    onSuccess: function (result) {
      console.log('access token + ' + result.getAccessToken().getJwtToken());
    },

    customChallenge: function (challengeParameters) {
      //gather user responses in challengeResponses based on challengeParameters
      cognitoUser.sendCustomChallengeAnswer(challengeResponses, this);
    },

    onFailure: function(err) {
      alert(err);
    },
});</code></pre> 
          <pre class="brush: js;"></pre> 
          <h1>Security considerations</h1> 
          <p>The custom user pool authentication flow works in parallel with all other user pool authentication flows, unless you specify otherwise. If you want to implement a custom flow that presents more challenges than, for example, USER_SRP_AUTH, you should choose <strong>Only allow Custom Authentication</strong> in the Amazon Cognito console, or include the CUSTOM_AUTH_FLOW_ONLY enum in the <span style="font-family: courier new,courier,monospace">ExplicitAuthFlows</span> user pool client property.</p> 
          <p><img class="alignnone wp-image-383 size-full" src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/0a57cb53ba59c46fc4b692527a38a87c78d84028/2016/10/25/flag_custom_auth.png" alt="flag_custom_auth" width="2024" height="1050"></p> 
          <h1>Conclusions</h1> 
          <p>As you can see, you can customize your authentication flow using the AWS Mobile SDKs. This enables you to create an experience that is designed to provide security and a user-friendly experience for your users. Wed like to hear how you plan to use this feature in your applications, so feel free to leave a comment to share other uses for this feature.</p> 
          <p>If you have comments or questions, please leave a comment, visit our&nbsp;<a href="https://forums.aws.amazon.com/forum.jspa?forumID=173" target="_blank">forums</a>, or post on <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/" target="_blank">Stack Overflow</a>.</p> 
         </section>
